    48	/**
    49	 * Jank instances are created from responsiveness values. Responsiveness is a profiler
    50	 * feature that can be turned on and off. When on, every sample includes a responsiveness
    51	 * value.
    52	 *
    53	 * This timing is captured by instrumenting the event queue. A runnable is added to the
    54	 * browser's event queue, then the profiler times how long it takes to come back.
    55	 * Generally, if this takes longer than some threshold, then this can be jank for the
    56	 * browser.
    57	 *
    58	 * This function converts those measurings of milliseconds into individual markers.
    59	 *
    60	 * For instance, take an array of responsiveness values:
    61	 *
    62	 *   [5, 25, 33, 3, 23, 42, 65, 71, 3, 10, 22, 31, 42, 3, 20, 40]
    63	 *           |___|              |___|              |___|
    64	 *     Runnable is reset    Jank of 71ms. The      Runnable reset under threshold.
    65	 *     but under 50ms,      responsiveness was
    66	 *     no jank.             reset from 71 to 3.
    67	 */
    68	export function deriveJankMarkers(
    69	  samples: SamplesTable,
    70	  thresholdInMs: number,
    71	  otherCategoryIndex: IndexIntoCategoryList
    72	): Marker[] {
    73	  const addMarker = () =>
    74	    jankInstances.push({
    75	      start: lastTimestamp - lastResponsiveness,
    76	      end: lastTimestamp,
    77	      name: 'Jank',
    78	      category: otherCategoryIndex,
    79	      threadId: null,
    80	      data: { type: 'Jank' },
    81	    });
    82	
    83	  let lastResponsiveness: number = 0;
    84	  let lastTimestamp: number = 0;
    85	  const jankInstances: Marker[] = [];
    86	  for (let i = 0; i < samples.length; i++) {
    87	    let currentResponsiveness;
    88	    if (samples.eventDelay) {
    89	      currentResponsiveness = samples.eventDelay[i];
    90	    } else if (samples.responsiveness) {
    91	      currentResponsiveness = samples.responsiveness[i];
    92	    }
    93	
    94	    if (currentResponsiveness === null || currentResponsiveness === undefined) {
    95	      // Ignore anything that's not numeric. This can happen if there is no responsiveness
    96	      // information, or if the sampler failed to collect a responsiveness value. This
    97	      // can happen intermittently.
    98	      //
    99	      // See Bug 1506226.
   100	      continue;
   101	    }
   102	    if (currentResponsiveness < lastResponsiveness) {
   103	      if (lastResponsiveness >= thresholdInMs) {
   104	        addMarker();
   105	      }
   106	    }
   107	    lastResponsiveness = currentResponsiveness;
   108	    lastTimestamp = samples.time[i];
   109	  }
   110	  if (lastResponsiveness >= thresholdInMs) {
   111	    addMarker();
   112	  }
   113	  return jankInstances;
   114	}
   115	
   116	export function getSearchFilteredMarkerIndexes(
   117	  getMarker: (MarkerIndex) => Marker,
   118	  markerIndexes: MarkerIndex[],
   119	  markerSchemaByName: MarkerSchemaByName,
   120	  searchRegExps: MarkerRegExps | null,
   121	  stringTable: StringTable,
   122	  categoryList: CategoryList
   123	): MarkerIndex[] {
   124	  if (!searchRegExps) {
   125	    return markerIndexes;
   126	  }
   127	
   128	  let hasPositiveRegexps = Boolean(searchRegExps.generic);
   129	  let hasNegativeRegexps = false;
   130	
   131	  for (const val of searchRegExps.fieldMap.values()) {
   132	    hasPositiveRegexps = hasPositiveRegexps || val.positive !== null;
   133	    hasNegativeRegexps = hasNegativeRegexps || val.negative !== null;
   134	  }
   135	
   136	  const newMarkers: MarkerIndex[] = [];
   137	  for (const markerIndex of markerIndexes) {
   138	    const marker = getMarker(markerIndex);
   139	    // Starting includeMarker with true in case `hasPositiveRegexps` is false.
   140	    // Otherwise it will be overwritten inside the next if branch.
   141	    let includeMarker = true;
   142	    // If there are positive RegExps, then check if the marker will be included.
   143	    if (hasPositiveRegexps) {
   144	      includeMarker = positiveFilterMarker(
   145	        marker,
   146	        markerSchemaByName,
   147	        searchRegExps,
   148	        stringTable,
   149	        categoryList
   150	      );
   151	    }
   152	
   153	    // If the marker marked as `included` so far by the positive regexps, check
   154	    // for negative RegExps and filter if there are any. If `includeMarker` is
   155	    // false here it means that it's already excluded so there is no point of
   156	    // checking it for negative filtering.
   157	    if (includeMarker && hasNegativeRegexps) {
   158	      includeMarker = negativeFilterMarker(
   159	        marker,
   160	        markerSchemaByName,
   161	        searchRegExps,
   162	        stringTable,
   163	        categoryList
   164	      );
   165	    }
   166	
   167	    if (includeMarker) {
   168	      newMarkers.push(markerIndex);
   169	    }
   170	  }
   171	
   172	  return newMarkers;
   173	}
   174	
   175	function positiveFilterMarker(
   176	  marker: Marker,
   177	  markerSchemaByName: MarkerSchemaByName,
   178	  searchRegExps: MarkerRegExps,
   179	  stringTable: StringTable,
   180	  categoryList: CategoryList
   181	): boolean {
   182	  // Need to assign it to a constant variable so Flow doesn't complain about
   183	  // passing it inside a function below.
   184	  const regExps = searchRegExps;
   185	
   186	  function test(value, key) {
   187	    key = key.toLowerCase();
   188	    const fieldRegexp = regExps.fieldMap.get(key);
   189	    const found =
   190	      (regExps.generic ? regExps.generic.test(value) : false) ||
   191	      (fieldRegexp && fieldRegexp.positive
   192	        ? fieldRegexp.positive.test(value)
   193	        : false);
   194	
   195	    // Reset regexp for each iteration. Otherwise state from previous
   196	    // iterations can cause matches to fail if the search is global or
   197	    // sticky.
   198	    if (regExps.generic) {
   199	      regExps.generic.lastIndex = 0;
   200	    }
   201	    if (fieldRegexp && fieldRegexp.positive) {
   202	      fieldRegexp.positive.lastIndex = 0;
   203	    }
   204	    return found;
   205	  }
   206	
   207	  const { data, name, category } = marker;
   208	
   209	  if (categoryList[category] !== undefined) {
   210	    const markerCategory = categoryList[category].name;
   211	    if (test(markerCategory, 'cat')) {
   212	      return true;
   213	    }
   214	  }
   215	
   216	  if (test(name, 'name')) {
   217	    return true;
   218	  }
   219	
   220	  if (data && typeof data === 'object') {
   221	    if (test(data.type, 'type')) {
   222	      // Check the type of the marker payload first.
   223	      return true;
   224	    }
   225	
   226	    // Now check the schema for the marker payload for searchable
   227	    const markerSchema = getSchemaFromMarker(markerSchemaByName, marker.data);
   228	    if (
   229	      markerSchema &&
   230	      markerPayloadMatchesSearch(markerSchema, marker, stringTable, test)
   231	    ) {
   232	      return true;
   233	    }
   234	  }
   235	
   236	  return false;
   237	}
   238	
   239	function negativeFilterMarker(
   240	  marker: Marker,
   241	  markerSchemaByName: MarkerSchemaByName,
   242	  searchRegExps: MarkerRegExps,
   243	  stringTable: StringTable,
   244	  categoryList: CategoryList
   245	): boolean {
   246	  // Need to assign it to a constant variable so Flow doesn't complain about
   247	  // passing it inside a function below.
   248	  const regExps = searchRegExps;
   249	
   250	  function test(value, key) {
   251	    key = key.toLowerCase();
   252	    const fieldRegexp = regExps.fieldMap.get(key);
   253	    const negativeRegexp = fieldRegexp?.negative;
   254	    if (!negativeRegexp) {
   255	      return false;
   256	    }
   257	
   258	    const found = negativeRegexp.test(value);
   259	
   260	    // Reset regexp for each iteration. Otherwise state from previous
   261	    // iterations can cause matches to fail if the search is global or
   262	    // sticky.
   263	    negativeRegexp.lastIndex = 0;
   264	    return found;
   265	  }
   266	
   267	  const { data, name, category } = marker;
   268	
   269	  if (categoryList[category] !== undefined) {
   270	    const markerCategory = categoryList[category].name;
   271	    if (test(markerCategory, 'cat')) {
   272	      // Found the category in the negative filters, do not include it.
   273	      return false;
   274	    }
   275	  }
   276	
   277	  if (test(name, 'name')) {
   278	    // Found the name in the negative filters, do not include it.
   279	    return false;
   280	  }
   281	
   282	  if (data && typeof data === 'object') {
   283	    if (test(data.type, 'type')) {
   284	      // Found the type of the payload in the negative filters, do not include it.
   285	      return false;
   286	    }
   287	
   288	    // Now check the schema for the marker payload for searchable
   289	    const markerSchema = getSchemaFromMarker(markerSchemaByName, marker.data);
   290	
   291	    if (
   292	      markerSchema &&
   293	      markerPayloadMatchesSearch(markerSchema, marker, stringTable, test)
   294	    ) {
   295	      // Found the field in the negative filters, do not include it.
   296	      return false;
   297	    }
   298	  }
   299	
   300	  return true;
   301	}
   302	
   303	/**
   304	 * This class is a specialized Map for IPC marker data, using the thread ID and
   305	 * marker index as the key, and storing IPCSharedData (which holds the start/end
   306	 * times for the IPC message.
   307	 */
   308	export class IPCMarkerCorrelations {
   309	  _correlations: Map<Tid, Map<number, IPCSharedData>>;
   310	
   311	  constructor() {
   312	    this._correlations = new Map();
   313	  }
   314	
   315	  set(tid: Tid, index: number, data: IPCSharedData): void {
   316	    let threadData = this._correlations.get(tid);
   317	    if (!threadData) {
   318	      threadData = new Map();
   319	      this._correlations.set(tid, threadData);
   320	    }
   321	    threadData.set(index, data);
   322	  }
   323	
   324	  get(tid: Tid, index: number): ?IPCSharedData {
   325	    const threadData = this._correlations.get(tid);
   326	    if (!threadData) {
   327	      return undefined;
   328	    }
   329	    return threadData.get(index);
   330	  }
   331	}
   332	
   333	/**
   334	 * This function correlates the sender and recipient sides of IPC markers so
   335	 * that we can share data between the two during profile processing.
   336	 *
   337	 * A single IPC message consists of 5 markers:
   338	 *
   339	 *        endpoint   (sender or background thread)
   340	 *            |      (or main thread in sender process if they are not profiled)
   341	 *            |
   342	 *            v
   343	 *     transferStart (IPC I/O thread in sender process)
   344	 *            |      (or main thread in sender process if it's not profiled)
   345	 *            |
   346	 *            v
   347	 *      transferEnd  (IPC I/O thread in sender process)
   348	 *            |      (or main thread in sender process if it's not profiled)
   349	 *            |
   350	 *            v
   351	 *      transferEnd  (IPC I/O thread in receiver process)
   352	 *            |      (or main thread in receiver process if it's not profiled)
   353	 *            |
   354	 *            v
   355	 *        endpoint   (receiver or background thread)
   356	 *                   (or main thread in receiver process if they are not profiled)
   357	 */
   358	export function correlateIPCMarkers(
   359	  threads: RawThread[],
   360	  shared: RawProfileSharedData
   361	): IPCMarkerCorrelations {
   362	  // Create a unique ID constructed from the source PID, destination PID,
   363	  // message seqno, and message type. Since the seqno is only unique for each
   364	  // message channel pair, we use the PIDs and message type as a way of
   365	  // identifying which channel pair generated this message.
   366	  function makeIPCMessageID(thread, data): string {
   367	    let pids;
   368	    if (data.direction === 'sending') {
   369	      pids = `${thread.pid},${data.otherPid}`;
   370	    } else {
   371	      pids = `${data.otherPid},${thread.pid}`;
   372	    }
   373	    return pids + `,${data.messageSeqno},${data.messageType}`;
   374	  }
   375	
   376	  function formatThreadName(tid: ?number): string | void {
   377	    if (tid !== null && tid !== undefined) {
   378	      const name = threadNames.get(tid);
   379	      if (name !== undefined) {
   380	        return `${name} (Thread ID: ${tid})`;
   381	      }
   382	    }
   383	    return undefined;
   384	  }
   385	
   386	  // Each IPC message has several (up to 5) markers associated with it. The
   387	  // order of these can be determined by the `direction` and `phase` attributes.
   388	  // To store all the markers for a given message, we convert the direction and
   389	  // phase to an index into an array.
   390	  function phaseToIndex(data: IPCMarkerPayload): number {
   391	    const { phase } = data;
   392	    if (data.direction === 'sending') {
   393	      switch (phase) {
   394	        case 'endpoint':
   395	        // We don't have a 'phase' field in the older profiles, in that case
   396	        // their phase is 'endpoint'. (fallthrough)
   397	        case undefined:
   398	          return 0;
   399	        case 'transferStart':
   400	          return 1;
   401	        case 'transferEnd':
   402	          return 2;
   403	        default:
   404	          throw assertExhaustiveCheck(phase, `Unhandled IPC phase type.`);
   405	      }
   406	    } else {
   407	      switch (phase) {
   408	        case 'transferEnd':
   409	          return 3;
   410	        case 'endpoint':
   411	        // We don't have a 'phase' field in the older profiles, in that case
   412	        // their phase is 'endpoint'. (fallthrough)
   413	        case undefined:
   414	          return 4;
   415	        case 'transferStart':
   416	          throw new Error(
   417	            'Unexpected "transferStart" phase found on receiving side.'
   418	          );
   419	        default:
   420	          throw assertExhaustiveCheck(phase, `Unhandled IPC phase type.`);
   421	      }
   422	    }
   423	  }
   424	
   425	  // Don't bother checking for IPC markers if the profile's string table
   426	  // doesn't have the string "IPC". This lets us avoid looping over all the
   427	  // markers when we don't have to.
   428	  const stringTable = StringTable.withBackingArray(shared.stringArray);
   429	  if (!stringTable.hasString('IPC')) {
   430	    return new IPCMarkerCorrelations();
   431	  }
   432	
   433	  // First, construct a mapping of marker IDs to an array of markers with that
   434	  // ID for faster lookup. We also collect the friendly thread names while we
   435	  // have access to all the threads. It's considerably more difficult to do
   436	  // this processing later.
   437	  const markersByKey: Map<
   438	    string,
   439	    Array<{ tid: number, index: number, data: IPCMarkerPayload } | void>,
   440	  > = new Map();
   441	  const threadNames: Map<number, string> = new Map();
   442	  for (const thread of threads) {
   443	    if (typeof thread.tid === 'number') {
   444	      const tid: number = thread.tid;
   445	      threadNames.set(tid, getFriendlyThreadName(threads, thread));
   446	
   447	      for (let index = 0; index < thread.markers.length; index++) {
   448	        const data = thread.markers.data[index];
   449	        if (!data || data.type !== 'IPC') {
   450	          continue;
   451	        }
   452	        const key = makeIPCMessageID(thread, data);
   453	        if (!markersByKey.has(key)) {
   454	          markersByKey.set(key, new Array(5).fill(undefined));
   455	        }
   456	
   457	        const currMarkers = ensureExists(markersByKey.get(key));
   458	        const phaseIdx = phaseToIndex(data);
   459	
   460	        if (currMarkers[phaseIdx] === undefined) {
   461	          currMarkers[phaseIdx] = { tid, index, data };
   462	        } else {
   463	          console.warn('Duplicate IPC marker found for key', key);
   464	        }
   465	      }
   466	    }
   467	  }
   468	
   469	  const correlations = new IPCMarkerCorrelations();
   470	  for (const markers of markersByKey.values()) {
   471	    const startEndpointMarker = markers[0];
   472	    const endEndpointMarker = markers[4];
   473	    const sendTid = startEndpointMarker ? startEndpointMarker.tid : undefined;
   474	    const recvTid = endEndpointMarker ? endEndpointMarker.tid : undefined;
   475	    const sharedData: IPCSharedData = {
   476	      startTime: startEndpointMarker
   477	        ? startEndpointMarker.data.startTime
   478	        : undefined,
   479	      sendStartTime: markers[1] ? markers[1].data.startTime : undefined,
   480	      sendEndTime: markers[2] ? markers[2].data.startTime : undefined,
   481	      recvEndTime: markers[3] ? markers[3].data.startTime : undefined,
   482	      endTime: endEndpointMarker ? endEndpointMarker.data.startTime : undefined,
   483	      sendTid,
   484	      recvTid,
   485	      sendThreadName: formatThreadName(sendTid),
   486	      recvThreadName: formatThreadName(recvTid),
   487	    };
   488	
   489	    const addedThreadIds = new Set();
   490	    if (startEndpointMarker) {
   491	      addedThreadIds.add(startEndpointMarker.tid);
   492	      correlations.set(
   493	        startEndpointMarker.tid,
   494	        startEndpointMarker.index,
   495	        sharedData
   496	      );
   497	    }
   498	    if (endEndpointMarker) {
   499	      addedThreadIds.add(endEndpointMarker.tid);
   500	      correlations.set(
   501	        endEndpointMarker.tid,
   502	        endEndpointMarker.index,
   503	        sharedData
   504	      );
   505	    }
   506	
   507	    // W<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. You should retry this tool after you have searched inside the file with `grep -n` in order to find the line numbers of what you are looking for.</NOTE>

     1	/* This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public
     2	 * License, v. 2.0. If a copy of the MPL was not distributed with this
     3	 * file, You can obtain one at http://mozilla.org/MPL/2.0/. */
     4	// @flow
     5	
     6	import * as React from 'react';
     7	
     8	import { Backtrace } from './Backtrace';
     9	import { TooltipDetailSeparator } from '../tooltip/TooltipDetails';
    10	import {
    11	  getCategoryPairLabel,
    12	  getFuncNamesAndOriginsForPath,
    13	  convertStackToCallNodeAndCategoryPath,
    14	} from 'firefox-profiler/profile-logic/profile-data';
    15	import { getFormattedTimelineValue } from 'firefox-profiler/profile-logic/committed-ranges';
    16	import {
    17	  formatMilliseconds,
    18	  formatPercent,
    19	} from 'firefox-profiler/utils/format-numbers';
    20	
    21	import type {
    22	  ImplementationFilter,
    23	  IndexIntoSamplesTable,
    24	  CategoryList,
    25	  Thread,
    26	  Milliseconds,
    27	} from 'firefox-profiler/types';
    28	import type { CpuRatioInTimeRange } from './thread/ActivityGraphFills';
    29	import { ensureExists } from '../../utils/flow';
    30	
    31	type CPUProps = CpuRatioInTimeRange;
    32	
    33	type RestProps = {|
    34	  +sampleIndex: IndexIntoSamplesTable,
    35	  +categories: CategoryList,
    36	  +rangeFilteredThread: Thread,
    37	  +implementationFilter: ImplementationFilter,
    38	|};
    39	
    40	type Props = {|
    41	  ...RestProps,
    42	  +cpuRatioInTimeRange: CPUProps | null,
    43	  +sampleIndex: IndexIntoSamplesTable | null,
    44	  +zeroAt: Milliseconds,
    45	  +profileTimelineUnit: string,
    46	  +interval: Milliseconds,
    47	|};
    48	
    49	/**
    50	 * Render thread CPU usage if it's present in the profile.
    51	 * This is split to reduce the rerender of the SampleTooltipRestContents component.
    52	 */
    53	class SampleTooltipCPUContents extends React.PureComponent<CPUProps> {
    54	  render() {
    55	    const { cpuRatio, timeRange } = this.props;
    56	
    57	    const percentageText = formatPercent(cpuRatio);
    58	    const cpuUsageAndPercentage = `${percentageText} (average over ${formatMilliseconds(
    59	      timeRange
    60	    )})`;
    61	
    62	    return (
    63	      <div className="tooltipDetails">
    64	        <div className="tooltipLabel">CPU:</div>
    65	        <div>{cpuUsageAndPercentage}</div>
    66	      </div>
    67	    );
    68	  }
    69	}
    70	
    71	/**
    72	 * Render the non-CPU related parts of the SampleTooltipContents.
    73	 */
    74	class SampleTooltipRestContents extends React.PureComponent<RestProps> {
    75	  render() {
    76	    const {
    77	      sampleIndex,
    78	      rangeFilteredThread,
    79	      categories,
    80	      implementationFilter,
    81	    } = this.props;
    82	    const { samples, stackTable } = rangeFilteredThread;
    83	    const stackIndex = samples.stack[sampleIndex];
    84	    if (stackIndex === null) {
    85	      return 'No stack information';
    86	    }
    87	    const categoryIndex = stackTable.category[stackIndex];
    88	    const subcategoryIndex = stackTable.subcategory[stackIndex];
    89	    const categoryColor = categories[categoryIndex].color;
    90	
    91	    return (
    92	      <>
    93	        <div className="tooltipDetails">
    94	          <div className="tooltipLabel">Category:</div>
    95	          <div>
    96	            <span
    97	              className={`colored-square category-color-${categoryColor}`}
    98	            />
    99	            {getCategoryPairLabel(categories, categoryIndex, subcategoryIndex)}
   100	          </div>
   101	        </div>
   102	        <div className="tooltipDetails">
   103	          <div className="tooltipLabel">Stack:</div>
   104	        </div>
   105	        <Backtrace
   106	          maxStacks={20}
   107	          stackIndex={stackIndex}
   108	          thread={rangeFilteredThread}
   109	          implementationFilter={implementationFilter}
   110	          categories={categories}
   111	        />
   112	      </>
   113	    );
   114	  }
   115	}
   116	
   117	/**
   118	 * This class displays the tooltip contents for a given sample. Typically the user
   119	 * will want to know what the function is, and its category.
   120	 */
   121	export class SampleTooltipContents extends React.PureComponent<Props> {
   122	  render() {
   123	    const {
   124	      cpuRatioInTimeRange,
   125	      sampleIndex,
   126	      rangeFilteredThread,
   127	      categories,
   128	      implementationFilter,
   129	      zeroAt,
   130	      profileTimelineUnit,
   131	      interval,
   132	    } = this.props;
   133	
   134	    let hasStack = false;
   135	    let formattedSampleTime = null;
   136	    if (sampleIndex !== null) {
   137	      const { samples, stackTable } = rangeFilteredThread;
   138	      const sampleTime = samples.time[sampleIndex];
   139	      const stackIndex = samples.stack[sampleIndex];
   140	      const hasSamples = samples.length > 0 && stackTable.length > 1;
   141	
   142	      if (hasSamples) {
   143	        const stack = getFuncNamesAndOriginsForPath(
   144	          convertStackToCallNodeAndCategoryPath(
   145	            rangeFilteredThread,
   146	            ensureExists(stackIndex)
   147	          ),
   148	          rangeFilteredThread
   149	        );
   150	        hasStack = stack.length > 1 || stack[0].funcName !== '(root)';
   151	      }
   152	
   153	      formattedSampleTime = getFormattedTimelineValue(
   154	        sampleTime - zeroAt,
   155	        profileTimelineUnit,
   156	        // Make sure that we show enough precision for the given sample interval.
   157	        interval / 10
   158	      );
   159	    }
   160	
   161	    return (
   162	      <>
   163	        {formattedSampleTime !== null ? (
   164	          <div className="tooltipDetails">
   165	            <div className="tooltipLabel">Sampled at:</div>
   166	            <div>{formattedSampleTime}</div>
   167	          </div>
   168	        ) : null}
   169	        {cpuRatioInTimeRange === null ? null : (
   170	          <SampleTooltipCPUContents
   171	            cpuRatio={cpuRatioInTimeRange.cpuRatio}
   172	            timeRange={cpuRatioInTimeRange.timeRange}
   173	          />
   174	        )}
   175	        {hasStack && cpuRatioInTimeRange !== null ? (
   176	          <TooltipDetailSeparator />
   177	        ) : null}
   178	        {!hasStack || sampleIndex === null ? null : (
   179	          <SampleTooltipRestContents
   180	            sampleIndex={sampleIndex}
   181	            rangeFilteredThread={rangeFilteredThread}
   182	            categories={categories}
   183	            implementationFilter={implementationFilter}
   184	          />
   185	        )}
   186	      </>
   187	    );
   188	  }

     1	/* This Source Code Form is subject to the terms of the Mozilla Public
     2	 * License, v. 2.0. If a copy of the MPL was not distributed with this
     3	 * file, You can obtain one at http://mozilla.org/MPL/2.0/. */
     4	
     5	// @flow
     6	
     7	import React from 'react';
     8	import classNames from 'classnames';
     9	import { filterCallNodeAndCategoryPathByImplementation } from 'firefox-profiler/profile-logic/transforms';
    10	import {
    11	  getFuncNamesAndOriginsForPath,
    12	  convertStackToCallNodeAndCategoryPath,
    13	} from 'firefox-profiler/profile-logic/profile-data';
    14	
    15	import type {
    16	  CategoryList,
    17	  Thread,
    18	  IndexIntoStackTable,
    19	  ImplementationFilter,
    20	} from 'firefox-profiler/types';
    21	
    22	import './Backtrace.css';
    23	
    24	type Props = {|
    25	  +thread: Thread,
    26	  // Tooltips will want to only show a certain number of stacks, while the sidebars
    27	  // can show all of the stacks.
    28	  +maxStacks: number,
    29	  +stackIndex: IndexIntoStackTable,
    30	  +implementationFilter: ImplementationFilter,
    31	  +categories: CategoryList,
    32	|};
    33	
    34	export function Backtrace(props: Props) {
    35	  const { stackIndex, thread, implementationFilter, maxStacks, categories } =
    36	    props;
    37	  const callNodePath = filterCallNodeAndCategoryPathByImplementation(
    38	    thread,
    39	    implementationFilter,
    40	    convertStackToCallNodeAndCategoryPath(thread, stackIndex)
    41	  );
    42	  const funcNamesAndOrigins = getFuncNamesAndOriginsForPath(
    43	    callNodePath,
    44	    thread
    45	  ).reverse();
    46	
    47	  if (funcNamesAndOrigins.length) {
    48	    return (
    49	      <ul className="backtrace">
    50	        {funcNamesAndOrigins
    51	          // Truncate the stacks
    52	          .slice(0, maxStacks)
    53	          .map(({ funcName, origin, isFrameLabel, category }, i) => (
    54	            <li
    55	              key={i}
    56	              className={classNames('backtraceStackFrame', {
    57	                backtraceStackFrame_isFrameLabel: isFrameLabel,
    58	              })}
    59	            >
    60	              <span
    61	                className={`colored-border category-color-${categories[category].color}`}
    62	                title={categories[category].name}
    63	              />
    64	              {funcName}
    65	              <em className="backtraceStackFrameOrigin">{origin}</em>
    66	            </li>
    67	          ))}
    68	        {funcNamesAndOrigins.length > maxStacks
    69	          ? [
    70	              <span
    71	                key={funcNamesAndOrigins.length}
    72	                className="colored-border ellipsis"
    73	              />,
    74	              '…',
    75	            ]
    76	          : null}
    77	      </ul>
    78	    );
    79	  }
    80	  return (
    81	    <div className="backtrace">
    82	      (The stack is empty because all of its frames are filtered out by the
    83	      implementation filter. Switch the implementation filter in the call tree
    84	      to see more frames.)
    85	    </div>
    86	  );
    87	}

    68	
    69	function _maybeFormatDuration(
    70	  start: number | void,
    71	  end: number | void
    72	): string {
    73	  if (start !== undefined && end !== undefined) {
    74	    return formatMilliseconds(end - start);
    75	  }
    76	  return 'unknown';
    77	}
    78	
    79	type OwnProps = {|
    80	  +markerIndex: MarkerIndex,
    81	  +marker: Marker,
    82	  +threadsKey: ThreadsKey,
    83	  +className?: string,
    84	  // In tooltips it can be awkward for really long and tall things to force
    85	  // the layout to be huge. This option when set to true will restrict the

   105	
   106	// Maximum image size of a tooltip field.
   107	const MAXIMUM_IMAGE_SIZE = 350;
   108	
   109	/**
   110	 * This component combines Marker Schema, and custom handling to generate tooltips
   111	 * for markers.
   112	 */
   113	class MarkerTooltipContents extends React.PureComponent<Props> {
   114	  _maybeRenderPageUrl = (): TooltipDetailComponent => {
   115	    const { pages, innerWindowIDToPageMap, marker } = this.props;
   116	
   117	    if (
   118	      !(
   119	        pages &&
   120	        innerWindowIDToPageMap &&
   121	        marker.data &&
   122	        marker.data.innerWindowID
   123	      )
   124	    ) {
   125	      return null;
   126	    }
   127	
   128	    const innerWindowID = marker.data.innerWindowID;
   129	    const page = innerWindowIDToPageMap.get(innerWindowID);
   130	
   131	    if (page) {
   132	      // If multiple pages have the same url, show the innerWindowID to disambiguate.
   133	      let innerWindowIDSuffix = null;
   134	      if (pages.filter((p) => p.url === page.url).length > 1) {
   135	        innerWindowIDSuffix = ' (id: ' + innerWindowID + ')';
   136	      }
   137	      try {
   138	        const { host } = new URL(page.url);
   139	        const hostIndex = page.url.indexOf(host);
   140	        if (hostIndex === -1) {
   141	          throw new Error(
   142	            'Unable to find the host in the URL. This is a programming error.'
   143	          );
   144	        }
   145	        const protocol = page.url.slice(0, hostIndex);
   146	        const rest = page.url.slice(hostIndex + host.length);
   147	        return (
   148	          <TooltipDetail label="Page">
   149	            <div className="tooltipDetailsUrl">
   150	              <span className="tooltipDetailsDim">{protocol}</span>
   151	              {host}
   152	              <span className="tooltipDetailsDim">{rest}</span>
   153	              {innerWindowIDSuffix}
   154	              {page.isPrivateBrowsing ? ' (private)' : null}
   155	            </div>
   156	          </TooltipDetail>
   157	        );
   158	      } catch (error) {
   159	        // Could not parse the URL. Just display the entire thing
   160	        let url = page.url;
   161	        if (innerWindowIDSuffix) {
   162	          url += innerWindowIDSuffix;
   163	        }
   164	        if (page.isPrivateBrowsing) {
   165	          url += ' (private)';
   166	        }
   167	        return <TooltipDetail label="Page">{url}</TooltipDetail>;
   168	      }
   169	    }
   170	    return null;
   171	  };
   172	
   173	  /**
   174	   * Either print the thread name that marker is in, or get the thread name from
   175	   * the threadId field if it's given. The second case is useful when a marker
   176	   * belongs to another thread but in this thread for some limitations in the
   177	   * platform side. For example, FileIO marker may belong to another thread if
   178	   * they have threadId field.
   179	   */
   180	  _renderThreadDetails(): TooltipDetailComponent[] {
   181	    const { marker, threadIdToNameMap } = this.props;
   182	    const data = marker.data;
   183	
   184	    // Markers might have threadId information if we're in a merged thread.
   185	    // Otherwise let's just take the thread information from the current thread.
   186	    const threadName =
   187	      marker.threadId !== null
   188	        ? threadIdToNameMap.get(marker.threadId)
   189	        : this.props.threadName;
   190	
   191	    if (data && data.threadId !== undefined) {
   192	      // This marker has some threadId data in its payload, which is about the
   193	      // thread where this event happened.
   194	      const threadId = data.threadId;
   195	      const occurringThreadName = threadIdToNameMap.get(threadId);
   196	
   197	      return [
   198	        <TooltipDetail label="Recording Thread" key="recording">
   199	          {threadName}
   200	        </TooltipDetail>,
   201	        // If we have the thread information of the occurring thread, then show.
   202	        // Otherwise, only show the thread ID.
   203	        occurringThreadName ? (
   204	          <TooltipDetail
   205	            label="Occurring Thread"
   206	            key="occurring"
   207	          >{`${occurringThreadName} (TID: ${threadId})`}</TooltipDetail>
   208	        ) : (
   209	          <TooltipDetail label="Occurring Thread ID" key="occurring">
   210	            {threadId}
   211	          </TooltipDetail>
   212	        ),
   213	      ];
   214	    }
   215	
   216	    // This is the common case.
   217	
   218	    return [
   219	      <TooltipDetail label="Track" key="thread">
   220	        {threadName}
   221	      </TooltipDetail>,
   222	    ];
   223	  }
   224	
   225	  /**
   226	   * This function combines the Marker Schema formatting, and custom handling of
   227	   * properties that are difficult to represent with the Schema.
   228	   */
   229	  _renderMarkerDetails(): TooltipDetailComponent[] {
   230	    const {
   231	      marker,
   232	      markerSchemaByName,
   233	      thread,
   234	      threadIdToNameMap,
   235	      processIdToNameMap,
   236	    } = this.props;
   237	    const data = marker.data;
   238	    const details: TooltipDetailComponent[] = [];
   239	
   240	    if (data) {
   241	      // Add the details for the markers based on their Marker schema.
   242	      const schema = getSchemaFromMarker(markerSchemaByName, marker.data);
   243	      if (schema) {
   244	        for (const field of schema.fields) {
   245	          if (field.hidden) {
   246	            // Do not include hidden fields.
   247	            continue;
   248	          }
   249	
   250	          const { key, label, format } = field;
   251	
   252	          const value = data[key];
   253	          if (value === undefined || value === null) {
   254	            // This marker doesn't have a value for this field. Values are optional.
   255	            continue;
   256	          }
   257	
   258	          details.push(
   259	            <TooltipDetail key={schema.name + '-' + key} label={label || key}>
   260	              {formatMarkupFromMarkerSchema(
   261	                schema.name,
   262	                format,
   263	                value,
   264	                thread.stringTable,
   265	                threadIdToNameMap,
   266	                processIdToNameMap
   267	              )}
   268	            </TooltipDetail>
   269	          );
   270	        }
   271	
   272	        if (schema.description) {
   273	          const key = schema.name + '-description';
   274	          details.push(
   275	            <TooltipDetail key={key} label="Description">
   276	              <div className="tooltipDetailsDescription">
   277	                {schema.description}
   278	              </div>
   279	            </TooltipDetail>
   280	          );
   281	        }
   282	      }
   283	
   284	      switch (data.type) {
   285	        case 'GCMinor': {
   286	          // The GC schema is mostly ignored.
   287	          details.push(...getGCMinorDetails(data));
   288	          break;
   289	        }
   290	        case 'GCMajor': {
   291	          // The GC schema is mostly ignored.
   292	          details.push(...getGCMajorDetails(data));
   293	          break;
   294	        }
   295	        case 'GCSlice': {
   296	          // The GC schema is mostly ignored.
   297	          details.push(...getGCSliceDetails(data));
   298	          break;
   299	        }
   300	        case 'Network': {
   301	          // Network markers embed lots of timing information inside of them, that
   302	          // must be reworked in the tooltip.
   303	          details.push(...getNetworkMarkerDetails(data));
   304	          break;
   305	        }
   306	        case 'IPC': {
   307	          // The logic to subtract times to create durations is not supported by
   308	          // the marker schema. Use custom handling for these in addition to
   309	          // the other properties supported by the Marker Schema.
   310	          details.push(
   311	            <TooltipDetail
   312	              label="Send Thread Latency"
   313	              key="IPC-Send Thread Latency"
   314	            >
   315	              {_maybeFormatDuration(data.startTime, data.sendStartTime)}
   316	            </TooltipDetail>,
   317	            <TooltipDetail
   318	              label="IPC Send Duration"
   319	              key="IPC-IPC Send Duration"
   320	            >
   321	              {_maybeFormatDuration(data.sendStartTime, data.sendEndTime)}
   322	            </TooltipDetail>,
   323	            <TooltipDetail label="IPC Recv Latency" key="IPC-IPC Recv Latency">
   324	              {_maybeFormatDuration(data.sendEndTime, data.recvEndTime)}
   325	            </TooltipDetail>,
   326	            <TooltipDetail
   327	              label="Recv Thread Latency"
   328	              key="IPC-Recv Thread Latency"
   329	            >
   330	              {_maybeFormatDuration(data.recvEndTime, data.endTime)}
   331	            </TooltipDetail>
   332	          );
   333	          break;
   334	        }
   335	        case 'CompositorScreenshot': {
   336	          if (data.url !== undefined) {
   337	            const { width, height } = computeScreenshotSize(
   338	              data,
   339	              MAXIMUM_IMAGE_SIZE
   340	            );
   341	            details.push(
   342	              <TooltipDetail label="Image" key="CompositorScreenshot-image">
   343	                <img
   344	                  className="tooltipScreenshotImg"
   345	                  src={thread.stringTable.getString(data.url)}
   346	                  style={{
   347	                    width,
   348	                    height,
   349	                  }}
   350	                />
   351	              </TooltipDetail>,
   352	              <TooltipDetail
   353	                label="Window Size"
   354	                key="CompositorScreenshot-window size"
   355	              >
   356	                <>
   357	                  {data.windowWidth}px × {data.windowHeight}px
   358	                </>
   359	              </TooltipDetail>,
   360	              <TooltipDetail
   361	                label="Description"
   362	                key="CompositorScreenshot-description"
   363	              >
   364	                This marker spans the time between each composite of a window
   365	                and shows the window contents during that time.
   366	              </TooltipDetail>,
   367	              <TooltipDetail
   368	                label="Window ID"
   369	                key="CompositorScreenshot-window id"
   370	              >
   371	                {data.windowID}
   372	              </TooltipDetail>
   373	            );
   374	          } else if (marker.name === 'CompositorScreenshotWindowDestroyed') {
   375	            details.push(
   376	              <TooltipDetail
   377	                label="Description"
   378	                key="CompositorScreenshot-description"
   379	              >
   380	                This marker shows the moment a window has been destroyed.
   381	              </TooltipDetail>,
   382	              <TooltipDetail
   383	                label="Window ID"
   384	                key="CompositorScreenshot-window id"
   385	              >
   386	                {data.windowID}
   387	              </TooltipDetail>
   388	            );
   389	          }
   390	          break;
   391	        }
   392	        default:
   393	        // Do nothing
   394	      }
   395	    }
   396	
   397	    return details;
   398	  }
   399	
   400	  _maybeRenderMarkerDuration() {
   401	    const { marker } = this.props;
   402	    if (marker.end === null) {
   403	      return null;
   404	    }
   405	
   406	    // We only know the duration if it's complete.
   407	    const duration = marker.incomplete
   408	      ? 'unknown duration'
   409	      : formatTimestamp(marker.end - marker.start, 3, 1);
   410	
   411	    return <div className="tooltipTiming">{duration}</div>;
   412	  }
   413	
   414	  _maybeRenderBacktrace() {
   415	    const {
   416	      marker,
   417	      thread,
   418	      implementationFilter,
   419	      restrictHeightWidth,
   420	      categories,
   421	    } = this.props;
   422	    const { data, start } = marker;
   423	    if (data && 'cause' in data && data.cause) {
   424	      const { cause } = data;
   425	      const causeAge = cause.time !== undefined ? start - cause.time : 0;
   426	      return [
   427	        <TooltipDetailSeparator key="backtrace-separator" />,
   428	        <TooltipDetail label="Stack" key="backtrace">
   429	          <div className="tooltipDetailsBackTrace">
   430	            {
   431	              /* The cause's time might be later than the marker's start. For
   432	                example this happens in some usual cases when the cause is
   433	                captured right when setting the end marker for tracing pairs of
   434	                markers. */
   435	              causeAge > 0 ? (
   436	                <h2 className="tooltipBackTraceTitle">
   437	                  {data.type === 'Styles' || marker.name === 'Reflow'
   438	                    ? `First invalidated ${formatTimestamp(
   439	                        causeAge
   440	                      )} before the flush, at:`
   441	                    : `Triggered ${formatTimestamp(causeAge)} ago, at:`}
   442	                </h2>
   443	              ) : null
   444	            }
   445	            <Backtrace
   446	              maxStacks={restrictHeightWidth ? 20 : Infinity}
   447	              stackIndex={cause.stack}
   448	              thread={thread}
   449	              implementationFilter={implementationFilter}
   450	              categories={categories}
   451	            />
   452	          </div>
   453	        </TooltipDetail>,
   454	      ];
   455	    }
   456	    return null;
   457	  }
   458	
   459	  _maybeRenderNetworkPhases() {
   460	    const {
   461	      marker: { data },
   462	      zeroAt,
   463	    } = this.props;
   464	    if (data && data.type === 'Network') {
   465	      return <TooltipNetworkMarkerPhases payload={data} zeroAt={zeroAt} />;
   466	    }
   467	    return null;
   468	  }
   469	
   470	  _renderTitle(): string {
   471	    const { markerIndex, getMarkerLabel } = this.props;
   472	    return getMarkerLabel(markerIndex);
   473	  }
   474	
   475	  /**
   476	   * Often-times component logic is split out into several different components. This
   477	   * is really helpful for interactive components, as each list of Props serves as
   478	   * a piece of memoization that can help with not over-rendering.
   479	   *
   480	   * This component is a little bit different, as it will only be rendered once per
   481	   * marker, as it's hovered. In addition, most of the complexity is in generating
   482	   * a list of TooltipDetailComponent, which are label/value pairs. Many parts
   483	   * of the tooltip are controlled by the Marker Schema, however there are some
   484	   * custom implementations for various markers that include some complexity.
   485	   * The general practice here is to provide functions of the signature:
   486	   *
   487	   * Payload => TooltipDetailComponent[]
   488	   *
   489	   * These TooltipDetailComponent are then combined with those generated by the
   490	   * Marker Schema.
   491	   *
   492	   * Finally, many sections are optional based on the data that is present. Note
   493	   * that these render function begin with "maybe", rather than embedded complicated
   494	   * ternaries everywhere. This leads to a style of render function that includes
   495	   * a short list of rendering strategies, in the order they appear.
   496	   */

  2916	/**
  2917	 * Return a function that can compare two samples' call nodes, and determine
  2918	 * which node is "before" the other.
  2919	 * We use the call node index for this order. In the call node table, call nodes
  2920	 * are ordered in depth-first traversal order, so we can just compare those
  2921	 * indexes.
  2922	 *
  2923	 * This order is used for the activity graph. The tree order comparator is used
  2924	 * specifically for hit testing, but we also compare call nodes in the same way
  2925	 * in mapCallNodeSelectedStatesToSamples, which is what gets used for determining
  2926	 * which areas of the graph to draw in with the selection highlight fill.
  2927	 *
  2928	 * "Ordered after" means "swims on top in the activity graph".
  2929	 *
  2930	 * The depth-first traversal order has the nice property that the nodes of a
  2931	 * subtree are located in a contiguous index range. This means that the
  2932	 * highlighted area for a selected subtree is contiguous in the graph.
  2933	 */
  2934	export function getTreeOrderComparator(

  2942	        callNodeInfoInverted
  2943	      )

  2945	}

Now I understand the issue. The problem is that when displaying marker stacks (like the "reflow" marker mentioned in the PR description), the code is using the function's start line number (`funcTable.lineNumber[funcIndex]`) instead of the actual frame line number where the function was called.

Looking at the code flow:
1. In `Marker.js`, the Backtrace component is used with `cause.stack` 
2. The Backtrace component calls `getFuncNamesAndOriginsForPath` 
3. `getFuncNamesAndOriginsForPath` calls `getOriginAnnotationForFunc` but doesn't pass any frame line numbers
4. `getOriginAnnotationForFunc` falls back to using the function's start line number when no frame line number is provided

The issue is that the stack frame information (which contains the actual line number where the function was called) is available in the stack table, but it's not being passed to the `getOriginAnnotationForFunc` function.

Let me search for where stack frame line numbers are stored and how to access them:

OBSERVATION:


/**
 * Frames contain the context information about the function execution at the moment in
 * time. The caller/callee relationship between frames is defined by the StackTable.
 */
export type FrameTable = {|
  // If this is a frame for native code, the address is the address of the frame's
  // assembly instruction,  relative to the native library that contains it.
  //
  // For frames obtained from stack walking, the address points into the call instruction.
  // It is not a return address, it is a "nudged" return address (i.e. return address
  // minus one byte). This is different from the Gecko profile format. The conversion
  // is performed at the end of profile processing. See the big comment above
  // nudgeReturnAddresses for more details.
  //
  // The library which this address is relative to is given by the frame's nativeSymbol:
  // frame -> nativeSymbol -> lib.
  address: Array<Address | -1>,

  // The inline depth for this frame. If there is an inline stack at an address,
  // we create multiple frames with the same address, one for each depth.
  // The outermost frame always has depth 0.
  //
  // Example:
  // If the raw stack is 0x10 -> 0x20 -> 0x30, and symbolication adds two inline frames
  // for 0x10, no inline frame for 0x20, and one inline frame for 0x30, then the

   219	export type FrameTable = {|
   220	  // If this is a frame for native code, the address is the address of the frame's
   221	  // assembly instruction,  relative to the native library that contains it.
   222	  //
   223	  // For frames obtained from stack walking, the address points into the call instruction.
   224	  // It is not a return address, it is a "nudged" return address (i.e. return address
   225	  // minus one byte). This is different from the Gecko profile format. The conversion
   226	  // is performed at the end of profile processing. See the big comment above
   227	  // nudgeReturnAddresses for more details.
   228	  //
   229	  // The library which this address is relative to is given by the frame's nativeSymbol:
   230	  // frame -> nativeSymbol -> lib.
   231	  address: Array<Address | -1>,
   232	
   233	  // The inline depth for this frame. If there is an inline stack at an address,
   234	  // we create multiple frames with the same address, one for each depth.
   235	  // The outermost frame always has depth 0.
   236	  //
   237	  // Example:
   238	  // If the raw stack is 0x10 -> 0x20 -> 0x30, and symbolication adds two inline frames
   239	  // for 0x10, no inline frame for 0x20, and one inline frame for 0x30, then the
   240	  // symbolicated stack will be the following:
   241	  //
   242	  // func:        outer1 -> inline1a -> inline1b -> outer2 -> outer3 -> inline3a
   243	  // address:     0x10   -> 0x10     -> 0x10     -> 0x20   -> 0x30   -> 0x30
   244	  // inlineDepth:    0   ->    1     ->    2     ->    0   ->    0   ->    1
   245	  //
   246	  // Background:
   247	  // When a compiler performs an inlining optimization, it removes a call to a function
   248	  // and instead generates the code for the called function directly into the outer
   249	  // function. But it remembers which instructions were the result of this inlining,
   250	  // so that information about the inlined function can be recovered from the debug
   251	  // information during symbolication, based on the instruction address.
   252	  // The compiler can choose to do inlining multiple levels deep: An instruction can
   253	  // be the result of a whole "inline stack" of functions.
   254	  // Before symbolication, all frames have depth 0. During symbolication, we resolve
   255	  // addresses to inline stacks, and create extra frames with non-zero depths as needed.
   256	  //
   257	  // The frames of an inline stack at an address all have the same address and the same
   258	  // nativeSymbol, but each has a different func and line.
   259	  inlineDepth: number[],
   260	
   261	  // The category of the frame. This is used to calculate the category of the stack nodes
   262	  // which use this frame:
   263	  // - If the frame has a null category, the stack node inherits its parent node's category
   264	  //   and subcategory. If there is no parent node, we use the "default category" (see ProfileMeta.categories).
   265	  // - If the frame has a non-null category, this category and subcategory is used for the stack node.
   266	  category: (IndexIntoCategoryList | null)[],
   267	
   268	  // The subcategory of a frame. This is used to calculate the subcategory of the stack nodes
   269	  // which use this frame.
   270	  // Must be non-null if the frame's category is non-null.
   271	  // Ignored if the frame's category is null.
   272	  // 0 is always a valid value and refers to the "Other" subcategory (see Category.subcategories).
   273	  subcategory: (IndexIntoSubcategoryListForCategory | null)[],
   274	
   275	  // The frame's function.
   276	  func: IndexIntoFuncTable[],
   277	
   278	  // The symbol index (referring into this thread's nativeSymbols table) corresponding
   279	  // to symbol that covers the frame address of this frame. Only non-null for native
   280	  // frames (e.g. C / C++ / Rust code). Null before symbolication.
   281	  nativeSymbol: (IndexIntoNativeSymbolTable | null)[],
   282	
   283	  // Inner window ID of JS frames. JS frames can be correlated to a Page through this value.
   284	  // It's used to determine which JS frame belongs to which web page so we can display
   285	  // that information and filter for single tab profiling.
   286	  // `0` for non-JS frames and the JS frames that failed to get the ID. `0` means "null value"
   287	  // because that's what Firefox platform DOM side assigns when it fails to get the ID or
   288	  // something bad happens during that process. It's not `null` or `-1` because that information
   289	  // is being stored as `uint64_t` there.
   290	  innerWindowID: (InnerWindowID | null)[],

   298	 * The funcTable stores the functions that were called in the profile.
   299	 * These can be native functions (e.g. C / C++ / rust), JavaScript functions, or
   300	 * "label" functions. Multiple frames can have the same function: The frame
   301	 * represents which part of a function was being executed at a given moment, and
   302	 * the function groups all frames that occurred inside that function.
   303	 * Concretely, for native code, each encountered instruction address is a separate
   304	 * frame, and the function groups all instruction addresses which were symbolicated
   305	 * with the same function name.
   306	 * For JS code, each encountered line/column in a JS file is a separate frame, and
   307	 * the function represents an entire JS function which can span multiple lines.
   308	 *
   309	 * Funcs that are orphaned, i.e. funcs that no frame refers to, do not have
   310	 * meaningful values in their fields. Symbolication will cause many funcs that
   311	 * were created upfront to become orphaned, as the frames that originally referred
   312	 * to them get reassigned to the canonical func for their actual function.
   313	 */
   314	export type FuncTable = {|
   315	  // The function name.
   316	  name: Array<IndexIntoStringTable>,
   317	
   318	  // isJS and relevantForJS describe the function type. Non-JavaScript functions
   319	  // can be marked as "relevant for JS" so that for example DOM API label functions
   320	  // will show up in any JavaScript stack views.
   321	  // It may be worth combining these two fields into one:
   322	  // https://github.com/firefox-devtools/profiler/issues/2543

   324	  relevantForJS: Array<boolean>,

   335	  // that information is stored in the frameTable, not in the funcTable.

  2155	export function convertStackToCallNodeAndCategoryPath(
  2156	  thread: Thread,
  2157	  stack: IndexIntoStackTable
  2158	): CallNodeAndCategoryPath {
  2159	  const { stackTable, frameTable } = thread;
  2160	  const path = [];
  2161	  for (
  2162	    let stackIndex = stack;
  2163	    stackIndex !== null;
  2164	    stackIndex = stackTable.prefix[stackIndex]
  2165	  ) {
  2166	    const index = stackTable.frame[stackIndex];
  2167	    path.push({
  2168	      category: stackTable.category[stackIndex],
  2169	      func: frameTable.func[index],
  2170	    });
  2171	  }
  2172	  return path.reverse();
  2173	}
  2174	
  2175	/**
  2176	 * Compute maximum depth of call stack for a given thread, and return maxDepth+1.
  2177	 * This value can be used as the length for any per-depth arrays.
  2178	 *
  2179	 * The depth for a root node is zero.
  2180	 * So if you only a single sample whose call node is a root node, this function
  2181	 * returns 1.
  2182	 *
  2183	 * If there are no samples, or the stacks are all filtered out for the samples,
  2184	 * then 0 is returned.
  2185	 */
  2186	export function computeCallNodeMaxDepthPlusOne(
  2187	  samples: SamplesLikeTable,
  2188	  callNodeInfo: CallNodeInfo
  2189	): number {
  2190	  // Compute the depth on a per-sample basis. This is done since the callNodeInfo is
  2191	  // computed for the filtered thread, but a samples-like table can use the preview
  2192	  // filtered thread, which involves a subset of the total call nodes.
  2193	  let maxDepth = -1;
  2194	  const callNodeTable = callNodeInfo.getNonInvertedCallNodeTable();
  2195	  // TODO: Use sampleCallNodes instead
  2196	  const stackIndexToCallNodeIndex =
  2197	    callNodeInfo.getStackIndexToNonInvertedCallNodeIndex();
  2198	  for (let sampleIndex = 0; sampleIndex < samples.length; sampleIndex++) {
  2199	    const stackIndex = samples.stack[sampleIndex];
  2200	    if (stackIndex === null) {
  2201	      continue;
  2202	    }
  2203	    const callNodeIndex = stackIndexToCallNodeIndex[stackIndex];
  2204	    const depth = callNodeTable.depth[callNodeIndex];
  2205	    if (depth > maxDepth) {
  2206	      maxDepth = depth;
  2207	    }
  2208	  }
  2209	
  2210	  return maxDepth + 1;
  2211	}
  2212	
  2213	/**
  2214	 * Compute the derived samples table.
  2215	 */
  2216	export function computeSamplesTableFromRawSamplesTable(
  2217	  rawSamples: RawSamplesTable,
  2218	  sampleUnits: SampleUnits | void,
  2219	  referenceCPUDeltaPerMs: number
  2220	): SamplesTable {

  2222	    responsiveness,

  2224	    stack,
  2225	    weight,
  2226	    weightType,
  2227	    threadId,
  2228	    length,
  2229	  } = rawSamples;
  2230	
  2231	  const timeDeltas =
  2232	    rawSamples.time !== undefined
  2233	      ? numberSeriesToDeltas(rawSamples.time)
  2234	      : ensureExists(rawSamples.timeDeltas);
  2235	  const threadCPURatio =
  2236	    sampleUnits !== undefined
  2237	      ? computeThreadCPURatio(
  2238	          rawSamples,
  2239	          sampleUnits,
  2240	          timeDeltas,
  2241	          referenceCPUDeltaPerMs
  2242	        )
  2243	      : undefined;
  2244	  const time = computeTimeColumnForRawSamplesTable(rawSamples);
  2245	
  2246	  return {
  2247	    // These fields are copied from the raw samples table:
  2248	    responsiveness,
  2249	    eventDelay,
  2250	    stack,

  console.log('"'"'   Function info length:'"'"', funcInfo.length);

  const rootFrameInfo = funcInfo[0];
  console.log('"'"'   Root function name:'"'"', rootFrameInfo.funcName);
  console.log('"'"'   Root function origin:'"'"', rootFrameInfo.origin);
  
  // The origin should contain the frame line number (10) not the function line number (1)
  if (rootFrameInfo.origin.includes('"'"':10'"'"')) {
    console.log('"'"'   ✓ Frame line number (10) is used in origin!'"'"');
  } else if (rootFrameInfo.origin.includes('"'"':1'"'"')) {
    console.log('"'"'   ✗ Function line number (1) is used instead of frame line number (10)!'"'"');
  } else {
    console.log('"'"'   ? Could not determine which line number is used'"'"');
  }
  
  console.log('"'"'\n3. Testing individual frame origins:'"'"');
  funcInfo.forEach((frame, index) => {
    const expectedFrameLine = mockThread.frameTable.line[index];
    const functionStartLine = mockThread.funcTable.lineNumber[mockThread.frameTable.func[index]];
    
    console.log(`   Frame ${index}:`);
    console.log(`     - Origin: ${frame.origin}`);
    console.log(`     - Expected frame line: ${expectedFrameLine}`);
    console.log(`     - Function start line: ${functionStartLine}`);
    
    if (frame.origin.includes(`:${expectedFrameLine}`)) {
      console.log(`     ✓ Correctly uses frame line number (${expectedFrameLine})`);
    } else if (frame.origin.includes(`:${functionStartLine}`)) {
      console.log(`     ✗ Incorrectly uses function start line (${functionStartLine}) instead of frame line (${expectedFrameLine})`);
    } else {
      console.log(`     ? Could not determine line number usage`);
    }
  });
  
  console.log('"'"'\n=== Test Summary ==='"'"');
  console.log('"'"'The fix should ensure that marker stacks display the line number'"'"');
  console.log('"'"'where the function was actually called (frame line number), not'"'"');
  console.log('"'"'the line number where the function starts (function line number).'"'"');
  
} catch (error) {
  console.error('"'"'Error running test:'"'"', error);
}'

// Test the getOriginAnnotationForFunc function logic
function getOriginAnnotationForFunc(funcIndex, funcTable, resourceTable, stringTable, frameLineNumber = null, frameColumnNumber = null) {
  let resourceType = null;
  let origin = null;
  const resourceIndex = funcTable.resource[funcIndex];
  if (resourceIndex !== -1) {
    resourceType = resourceTable.type[resourceIndex];
    const resourceNameIndex = resourceTable.name[resourceIndex];
    origin = stringTable.getString(resourceNameIndex);
  }

  const fileNameIndex = funcTable.fileName[funcIndex];
  let fileName;
  if (fileNameIndex !== null) {
    fileName = stringTable.getString(fileNameIndex);

    // Simplified parse function for testing
    fileName = fileName.split('"'"'?'"'"')[0]; // Simple path parsing

    if (frameLineNumber !== null) {
      fileName += '"'"':'"'"' + frameLineNumber;
      if (frameColumnNumber !== null) {
        fileName += '"'"':'"'"' + frameColumnNumber;
      }
    } else {
      const lineNumber = funcTable.lineNumber[funcIndex];
      if (lineNumber !== null) {
        fileName += '"'"':'"'"' + lineNumber;
        const columnNumber = funcTable.columnNumber[funcIndex];
        if (columnNumber !== null) {
          fileName += '"'"':'"'"' + columnNumber;
        }
      }
    }
  }

  if (fileName) {
    if (origin) {
      return `${origin}: ${fileName}`;
    }
    return fileName;
  }

  if (origin) {
    return origin;
  }

  return '"'"''"'"';
}

+// Simple test to verify that the line number fix logic is correct
+
+// Test the getOriginAnnotationForFunc function logic
+function getOriginAnnotationForFunc(funcIndex, funcTable, resourceTable, stringTable, frameLineNumber = null, frameColumnNumber = null) {
+  let resourceType = null;
+  let origin = null;
+  const resourceIndex = funcTable.resource[funcIndex];
+  if (resourceIndex !== -1) {
+    resourceType = resourceTable.type[resourceIndex];
+    const resourceNameIndex = resourceTable.name[resourceIndex];
+    origin = stringTable.getString(resourceNameIndex);
+  }
+
+  const fileNameIndex = funcTable.fileName[funcIndex];
+  let fileName;
+  if (fileNameIndex !== null) {
+    fileName = stringTable.getString(fileNameIndex);
+
+    // Simplified parse function for testing
+    fileName = fileName.split('?')[0]; // Simple path parsing
+
+    if (frameLineNumber !== null) {
+      fileName += ':' + frameLineNumber;
+      if (frameColumnNumber !== null) {
+        fileName += ':' + frameColumnNumber;
+      }
+    } else {
+      const lineNumber = funcTable.lineNumber[funcIndex];
+      if (lineNumber !== null) {
+        fileName += ':' + lineNumber;
+        const columnNumber = funcTable.columnNumber[funcIndex];
+        if (columnNumber !== null) {
+          fileName += ':' + columnNumber;
+        }
+      }
+    }
+  }
+
+  if (fileName) {
+    if (origin) {
+      return `${origin}: ${fileName}`;
+    }
+    return fileName;
+  }
+
+  if (origin) {
+    return origin;
+  }
+
+  return '';
+}
+
+// Mock data that represents the actual scenario
+const mockData = {
+  funcTable: {
+    fileName: [0, 1], // indices into string table
+    lineNumber: [24, 10], // Function start line numbers 
+    columnNumber: [0, 0],
+    resource: [-1, -1],
+    length: 2
+  },
+  frameTable: {
+    line: [50, 100], // Frame line numbers (where the function was called)
+    column: [5, 10], // Frame column numbers
+    length: 2
+  },
+  stringTable: {
+    getString: (index) => index === 0 ? 'http://example.com/test.js' : 'http://example.com/other.js'
+  },
+  resourceTable: {
+    type: [],
+    name: [],
+    length: 0
+  }
+};
+
+console.log('Testing marker stack line number fix...\n');
+
+// Test case 1: Without frame line numbers (old behavior)
+console.log('1. Test WITHOUT frame line numbers (OLD BEHAVIOR):');
+const oldResult = getOriginAnnotationForFunc(
+  0, // funcIndex
+  mockData.funcTable,
+  mockData.resourceTable,
+  mockData.stringTable
+);
+console.log('   Result:', oldResult);
+console.log('   Shows function start line: 24 (incorrect for marker stacks)\n');
+
+// Test case 2: With frame line numbers (new behavior)
+console.log('2. Test WITH frame line numbers (NEW BEHAVIOR):');
+const newResult = getOriginAnnotationForFunc(
+  0, // funcIndex
+  mockData.funcTable,
+  mockData.resourceTable,
+  mockData.stringTable,
+  50, // frameLineNumber (where the function was actually called)
+  5   // frameColumnNumber
+);
+console.log('   Result:', newResult);
+console.log('   Shows frame line: 50 (correct for marker stacks)\n');
+
+// Test case 3: Another function with different line numbers
+console.log('3. Test another function WITH frame line numbers:');
+const anotherResult = getOriginAnnotationForFunc(
+  1, // funcIndex
+  mockData.funcTable,
+  mockData.resourceTable,
+  mockData.stringTable,
+  100, // frameLineNumber (where the function was actually called)
+  10   // frameColumnNumber
+);
+console.log('   Result:', anotherResult);
+console.log('   Shows frame line: 100 (correct for marker stacks)\n');
+
+console.log('=== SUMMARY ===');
+console.log('✓ The fix ensures that marker stacks display the line number');
+console.log('  where the function was actually called (frame line number),');
+console.log('  not where the function starts (function line number).');
+console.log('');
+console.log('For the example in the PR description:');
+console.log('- Before: Line number 24 (where function starts)');
+console.log('- After:  Line number 50 (where function was called)');
